Click on ‘Save Token’ button On the list, you will see the details of token. Every token will have a URL. Use the URL to open the Customer details form The Customer will have to fill in the details and then click on Take Survey to open the survey. To edit, copy or delete the token you can click edit, copy or delete link in the action column What if I edit the Token or Delete the token? Does the data collected will be lost? No. If you edit or delete the token the previously collected responses will remain stored in the raw data. How to check the data collected through Open URL? You can go into Raw Data to view the responses collected through anonymous link. In the Raw data, you will see the responses with the external reference ‘Survey_Token’. Does this data also get collected on dashboard? Yes, the data collected is stored on Dashboard. Only the Completion and Completion Trend widgets do not show the count for Anonymous responses.       "content": "Anonymous tokens Anonymous tokens are the type of survey tokens wherein respondents can access the survey (either by survey URL or QR code) and respond anonymously. These tokens don't require any personal details to be entered before responding to the survey. How can I add anonymous tokens to my account? Once you are logged in to your account, go to Deploy >> Survey Token >> Anonymous Token and click on the Add button provided. It will open a Add Anonymous Survey Token pop-up where you can enter the required details such as token name, segment for which you want to create the token, select the survey for which you want to create the token, enter the timeframe start-date end-date for which you want the token to be active along with other details and click on Save button. It will add the anonymous token to the tokens list. Quota - Using this you can set the maximum number of responses to be taken using this token Product Group and Product - You can set the product group and product for which you want to take the responses Custom variables - 5 custom variables are supported using which you can pass additional information along with the token. This information will be saved in the respective custom variables in the response viewer table. Utilize Email from Question - This option allows you to use the email address provided by the respondent in the survey as their designated contact for the response. It will also be utilized in other CX tools, such as Enhanced Closedloop Feedback, where the email will be used to generate tickets, enabling further actions to be taken. By default it will be off. For this feature to be enabled, an email-type question must be included in the survey, as the system relies solely on this question type for configuration How can I add multiple anonymous survey tokens at once? Click on the Bulk Add button provided within the Anonymous tokens. It will open a pop-up where you can download an Excel file format to upload the anonymous survey tokens in bulk. Once downloaded, you can enter all the requested details and save the file. Each row in the Excel file will be added as a separate token to the system. You can choose this file and press the Upload button which will upload this file to the system and create anonymous tokens based on the information present in the file. Can I download all the anonymous token details in one go? Yes, using the Download button provided in the platform you can download details of all the anonymous tokens present in the account. It will be downloaded in Excel file format with a dedicated column for the token URL. How can I edit or delete the created anonymous survey tokens? You can edit, or delete a survey token using the provided action buttons along with the survey token. How to check the data collected through Open URL? You can go into Raw Data to view the responses collected through anonymous link. In the Raw data, you will see the responses with the external reference Survey_Token. What if I edit the Token or Delete the token? Does the data collected will be lost? No. If you edit or delete the token the previously collected responses will remain stored in the raw data.       "id": "customer-experience/transactional-tokens",
      "product": "CX",
      "title": "Transactional tokens",

      "url": "https://www.questionpro.com/help/customer-experience/transactional-tokens.html",

          "text": "Transactional Tokens"
        }
      ],
      "steps": [],
      "content": "Transactional Tokens With the transactional tokens you can take the responses in real time; you need to setup your business hierarchy and then you can create survey tokens for each segment present within the workspace. It is a sharable link that you can keep ready on the handheld devices. With transactional tokens, you can ask users to enter relevant information before starting a survey. Once the respondent fills information, the system checks the workflow set in the system, and as per the workflow setup transaction is created and a survey invitation is sent to the respondent using which the respondent can respond to the survey. How to create a transactional token? Once you are logged into CX, go to Deploy>> Survey Token >> Transactional Token It will open a “Add Transactional Survey Token” popup, where you can add the required details such as token name, choose the segment for which you want to create the token, add logo, and others. Switch on the toggle for the fields that you need your customers to fill out before taking the survey. Once you click on the Save button it will add a token to the transactional tokens list with the token URL. How to access the token and share the survey using it? You can click on this token link to access the transactional token and this link can also be saved on other handheld devices for enhanced accessibility and sharing. This token URL can be shared with the customers whom you want to respond to the survey. Once the customers click on the survey token they are prompted to fill in the required details; post that, they can click on the “Take Survey” button to open the survey. The system will not allow to take the survey if any exclude rules are set for the segments chosen. To edit, copy the URL or delete the token you can click edit, copy or delete buttons in the action column How to check the data collected through Open URL? You can go into Raw Data to view the responses collected through anonymous link. In the Raw data, you will see the responses with the external reference ‘Survey_Token’. What if I edit the Token or Delete the token? Does the data collected will be lost? No. If you edit or delete the token the previously collected responses will remain stored in the raw data.       "content": "Trigger Rules Settings Overview Trigger rules are used to control when and to whom an intercept is shown. You can define conditions based on user behavior, session activity, and environment. Rules are configured as a flat list: Each intercept contains individual rules You can apply only one logic type: AND or OR AND: All conditions must be met OR: Any condition can be met How to add a new rule To add a new rule: Open the intercept where you want to configure targeting Click the Add Rule button Select the rule type and define the condition This allows you to configure when the intercept should be triggered. What types of rules can you use to target intercepts? The platform offers a range of rule types to tailor intercept targeting: Country: Trigger intercepts based on the visitor’s geographic location. Browser Type: Target users according to the browser they are using, such as Chrome, Firefox, Safari, or Edge. Device Type: Segment users based on their device category, including Mobile, Tablet, or Desktop. Operating System: Restrict intercepts to users operating on specific systems (e.g., Windows, macOS, iOS, Android). Button: Trigger an intercept when a designated button is clicked, identified using its HTML ID. Example: Pay Now Entering the ID pay will trigger the intercept upon the button click. Page URL: Configure intercepts for specific pages using URL-based conditions. Supported operators include Equals, Not Equals, Includes, and Excludes. Session Duration: Trigger an intercept after a visitor has spent a specified amount of time on the website. User Type: Target users based on their visit history: New visitors Returning visitors User classification is determined using browser cookies. Note: Cookie expiration can be configured in Project Settings. Once expired, users are treated as new visitors. URL Parameter: Trigger intercepts based on values present in URL query parameters. IP Address: Include or exclude users based on their IP address. Data Layer: Leverage variables defined within your website’s data layer to trigger intercepts. Example: If user.plan = premium, the intercept will be displayed. Variable naming formats: ObjectName.VariableName VariableName (global) Pages Visited: Trigger intercepts based on the number of pages viewed within the current session. Example: Display an intercept after a user has visited three pages. Scroll Depth: Trigger intercepts based on how far a visitor has scrolled on a webpage. This allows you to engage users after they have viewed a specific portion of the content. Example: Display an intercept when a user scrolls 50% or 75% down the page. HTML Selector: Trigger intercepts based on user interaction with specific HTML elements identified via CSS selectors. Examples: #signup-button, .menu-item Total Visits: Trigger intercepts based on the total number of visits a user has made to the website, tracked using browser cookies. Example: Display an intercept only on the user’s second or third visit. Rule Type Variable Details Supported Operands Values Country Equals to, Not equals to All Countries Browser Type Equals to, Not equals to Chrome, Firefox, Safari, Edge Device Type Equals to, Not equals to Mobile, Tablet, Desktop Operating System Equals to, Not equals to Windows, macOS, Linux, Android, iOS Button Equals to HTML Button ID Page URL Equals to, Not equals to, Includes, Excludes Page URL Session Duration Greater than Time (MM:SS) User Type Equals to New visitor, Returning visitor URL Parameter Parameter name Equals to, Not equals to, Includes, Excludes Parameter value IP Address Equals to, Not equals to, Includes, Excludes, Between IP address Data Layer objectName.variableName Equals to, Not equals to, Includes, Excludes Variable value Pages Visited Greater than, Equals to Number of pages HTML Selector CSS Selector Equals to Element selector (ID/Class) Total Visits Greater than, Equals to Number of visits License This feature is available with the following license : Customer Experience Was the article helpful?     {
      "id": "customer-experience/HTML-Element-Trigger-Rule",
      "product": "CX",
      "title": "HTML Element Rule",
      "summary": "Learn how to use the HTML Selector targeting rule to trigger surveys based on specific page elements.",
      "url": "https://www.questionpro.com/help/customer-experience/HTML-Element-Trigger-Rule.html",
      "scraped_at": "2026-06-17T12:06:13.893Z",
      "headings": [
        {
          "level": "H1",
          "text": "HTML Selector Targeting Rule"
        }
      ],
      "steps": [],
      "content": "HTML Selector Targeting Rule The HTML Selector Targeting Rule allows you to trigger Intercept surveys based on specific elements on your webpage using HTML selectors such as IDs or classes. This enables more precise, contextual, and behavior-driven survey delivery. Why use the HTML Selector rule? Traditional targeting rules like URL, time on page, or device type do not always capture moments tied to specific page elements. Many important user interactions such as viewing pricing, encountering an error message, or reaching a content block occur within specific HTML elements. Using the HTML Selector rule helps you trigger surveys exactly when these elements appear on page load, making surveys more relevant and improving response rates. How to add an HTML Selector rule? To add an HTML Selector rule: Navigate to Intercept » Rule Group Select HTML Selector from the rule dropdown Enter your HTML selector (e.g., #task, .product-title) Select an operand (Equals, Not Equals, Includes, Excludes, Exists) Enter a text value to compare Save the rule The selector supports valid querySelector(). The maximum input length for selectors and values is 255 characters. What operands are available? Equals: Matches the element’s text exactly. Not Equals: Works when the element’s text does not exactly match the value. Includes: True if the element’s text contains the value (partial match). Excludes: True if the element’s text does not contain the value. Exists: Works when the element exists in the DOM. No value needed. Technical limitations First Match Priority: Only the first matching element in the DOM is evaluated. One-Time Scan on Page Load: The rule is checked once when the page loads. It does not re-check dynamically added or updated content. Plain Text Only: The targeted element must contain plain text only. Nested HTML elements are not supported. Supported Selectors: IDs (#task) and classes (.product-title) are supported. Use cases The HTML Selector rule helps you target surveys at precise moments tied to specific on-page content. Some common scenarios include: Triggering a survey when a user reaches a Pricing section identified by a unique ID. Showing a survey on specific product pages by detecting product title or detail elements via class selectors. Displaying a survey when an error message or alert banner appears, allowing real-time feedback after user friction. Triggering feedback when a promotional or feature section loads, helping measure responses to new content.       "content": "Mobile Intercept Settings Configure intercept settings to deliver a seamless experience for mobile users. These settings help boost engagement, improve response accuracy, and create a more personalized survey experience. Intercept Settings: Allow Multiple Responses The Allow Multiple Responses setting lets you control whether visitors can respond to the intercept more than once. How to Enable Multiple Responses: Go to the Intercept Settings tab for your intercept Toggle the Allow Multiple Responses switch to ON Click Save Changes Intercept Settings: Trigger Delay The Trigger Delay setting allows you to set a time delay (in seconds) before the intercept appears after a visitor lands on your website. How to Set a Trigger Delay: Go to the Intercept Settings tab for your intercept In the Trigger Delay field, enter the number of seconds you’d like to delay the intercept popup Click Save Changes Intercept Settings: Display Sample Rate The Display Sample Rate setting lets you control how often a mobile intercept is shown to eligible users. It defines the percentage of users who meet your targeting rules and will actually see the intercept. This helps prevent over-surveying, protects the mobile experience, and allows you to manage response volume or run controlled experiments. How to Configure Display Sample Rate: Go to the Intercept Settings tab for your intercept In the Display Sample Rate field, enter the percentage of eligible users who should see the intercept Click Save Changes Best Practices: Start with a lower sample rate (for example, 10–20%) during testing phases. Gradually increase the rate after validating performance and user experience. Combine Display Sample Rate with targeting rules for precise survey distribution. Use sampling to avoid interrupting too many user sessions in high-traffic areas of your app. What are Language-Specific Intercepts in the SDK? The Mobile Intercept SDK supports language-specific intercepts that automatically localize the survey experience based on the mobile device’s language settings. If a translation for the detected language is available in the survey, it will be used. Otherwise, the intercept defaults to English. This ensures that users receive surveys in their preferred language, enhancing engagement and response quality. How Language Detection Works in the SDK The SDK reads the mobile device's default language (e.g., fr for French). If the corresponding translation is present in the survey, the intercept will be shown in that language. If no translation is available, the SDK displays the intercept in English. Example: If a user's phone is set to Spanish and the survey has a Spanish translation, the intercept will be presented in Spanish. How to Enable Language-Specific Intercepts Log in to your admin dashboard and navigate to the Intercept Settings. Toggle the option Enable Language-Specific Intercepts to ON. Click Save Changes to apply the setting. Once enabled, the SDK will automatically handle language selection at runtime. Pre-Requisites for Language-Specific Intercepts The associated survey must include all necessary language translations. Translations should be reviewed and validated for accuracy. To learn how to add and manage translations, refer to: How to Create Multilingual Surveys License This feature is available with the following license : Customer Experience Was the article helpful? This guide introduces the concept of Journey Management, explains why it matters, and shows how QuestionPro Journey Management helps you move from static journey maps to continuous, data-driven experience management. What is Journey Management? Journey Management is the practice of designing, monitoring, and continuously improving customer journeys using real data, insights, and operational signals. Unlike traditional journey mapping - where journeys are created as one-time visual diagrams - QuestionPro Journey Management treats journeys as living, evolving systems that reflect how customers actually move through experiences. Visualize end-to-end customer experiences Measure what is happening at each stage and step Identify friction, pain points, and moments of truth Prioritize improvements based on impact Track outcomes and business results Why do traditional journey maps fall short? Many organizations invest in journey maps, but those maps often: Become outdated quickly Live in slide decks or whiteboards Are disconnected from real customer data Do not drive action Traditional mapping tools focus on visualization, while feedback tools focus on measurement. Because these tools are separate, teams can see feedback but not where it fits in the journey, and see journeys but not how they are performing. What is QuestionPro Journey Management? QuestionPro Journey Management is a purpose-built platform for designing and managing complex journey frameworks while natively integrating: Voice of Customer (VoC) data Experience metrics such as NPS, CSAT, and CES Research insights AI-powered analysis Actions and initiatives It transforms static journey maps into interactive, data-driven management systems that support continuous improvement. What makes QuestionPro Journey Management different? QuestionPro Journey Management unifies journey design, measurement, insights, and action in a single system. Instead of only answering: What does the journey look like? You can also answer: Which steps are underperforming? What pain points drive dissatisfaction or churn? Which personas are impacted? What initiatives are in progress? Are improvements delivering results? How does QuestionPro Journey Management work? Design journey maps that represent your customer experience Structure journeys using stages, steps, and lanes Connect data sources, metrics, and insights to journey elements Use AI to surface themes, pain points, and root causes Create initiatives to address issues Track progress, outcomes, and ROI Key capabilities Scalable journey frameworks Native metrics integration AI-powered insights AI-driven personas Native insight dashboards Actionable outer loop (initiatives) Backlog and ROI tracking Real-time collaboration Who is QuestionPro Journey Management for? CX and UX teams Product managers Research and insights teams Service design teams Operations and transformation teams It is built for organizations that want to manage experiences, not just map them.       "content": "Journey Map Building Blocks: Stages, Steps, and Lanes What are the building blocks of a journey map? Journey maps are structured using three key building blocks: Stages, Steps, and Lanes. These components help you organize the customer experience into clear phases, actions, and perspectives, making it easier to analyze and improve journeys end to end. Watch this video for a quick overview of journey map building blocks and how to add stages, steps, and lanes while editing a journey map. Your browser does not support the video tag. What are stages, steps, and lanes? Stages represent the high-level phases of the journey, such as onboarding, usage, or support. Steps capture the individual actions, touchpoints, or moments that occur within each stage. Lanes run horizontally across the journey map and are used to organize different types of information, such as customer actions, emotions, pain points, or internal ownership. How do I add stages and steps to a journey map? Step 1: Open the journey map you want to edit. Step 2: Hover over an existing stage or step name in the journey map. Step 3: When you hover, a + (add) button appears next to the stage or step name. Step 4: Click the + button to add a new stage or step. Step 5: Enter a name for the new stage or step to continue building your journey. How do I add lanes to a journey map? Step 1: Open the journey map in edit mode. Step 2: Hover your cursor between any two existing lanes. Step 3: A + (add) button appears between the lanes. Step 4: Click the + button to add a new lane. Step 5: Name the lane and use it to capture relevant information across the journey. Can I add or modify stages, steps, and lanes later? Yes. You can add, update, or reorganize stages, steps, and lanes at any time while editing a journey map. This flexibility allows you to refine your journey as new insights and requirements emerge. The Layers feature allows users to create a custom view of their journey maps by selecting specific lanes and columns. These Layers help users focus on relevant portions of complex journey maps without having to view the entire map each time. Each Layer can be named, saved, and viewed independently. Layers are optimized for screenshot capture, making it easy to insert journey insights into presentations or reports. Watch this video to learn how to use Layers in QuestionPro Journey Management to customize journey maps for different perspectives and focus on the insights that matter most to each team. Your browser does not support the video tag. How do you create a Layer in a journey map? Navigate to your desired journey map. Click on the Layers button. Enter a name for the Layer and click Apply. Your new Layer will now appear under the Layers dropdown for quick access and reuse. How do you access and switch between Layers? All created Layers are available under the Layers dropdown, and you can switch between any of these Layers. Select any saved Layer to load its custom view instantly. The active Layer’s name is displayed for easy reference while viewing. What is the base Layer? The base Layer is the default view of the entire journey map. It cannot be edited or renamed. All user-created Layers are nested under the base Layer for easy reference and access. How do you manage saved Layers? Saved Layers are always accessible under the selected journey map. Why are interviews important for mapping customer journeys? Customer interviews provide rich qualitative insight that cannot be captured through surveys or analytics alone. The system analyzes the uploaded content, shows a preview of the detected structure, and lets you adjust the mappings before creating the journey. Watch this video to learn how AI-Assisted Import Maps automatically convert your files into journey maps using AI. Your browser does not support the video tag. How do I import a journey map using AI? To import a journey map using AI, follow these steps: Go to Journey Management. Open Settings » Import. Choose the Workspace and Board where the journey should be created. Select one or more files using the Choose file button. You can upload Excel (.xlsx) files for structured journey data and PDF (.pdf) files. Click Import. The system analyzes all selected files together and generates a unified journey map. What happens after import? After import, the journey map is configured automatically: A new journey map is created in the selected board. Stages appear as the main lifecycle sections identified across the uploaded files. Steps appear within their respective stages. Lanes appear as swimlanes based on detected roles, themes, or categories. Information from multiple files is consolidated into a single visualization. You can edit, rename, or extend the journey like any other journey map. Frequently Asked Questions The following questions address common usage scenarios, limitations, and best practices for using AI-Assisted Journey Map Import. What file formats can I upload for AI-Assisted Journey Map Import? You can currently upload Excel and PDF files to generate journey maps. Support for PowerPoint files and ZIP uploads is planned for an upcoming release. Do I need to follow a specific template before uploading my file? No strict template is required. The AI reads and interprets your structure automatically, identifying stages, steps, and lanes. However, cleaner formatting such as clear headers and consistent columns will improve mapping accuracy. How accurate is QuestionProAI when converting my file into a journey map? QuestionProAI is designed to preserve your structure and context with high accuracy by automatically identifying stages, steps, and lanes from your file. After generation, you can review and refine the journey directly in the editor to make any adjustments needed. Can I edit the journey after it has been generated? Yes. Once imported, the journey behaves like any other journey in Journey Management: Add or remove stages Modify steps or lanes Enhance with insights, ownership, or metrics Will this overwrite any existing journeys? No. Imports always create new journey maps inside your selected workspace and board. Your existing journeys remain unchanged. Is this feature included in my subscription, or does it cost extra? AI-Assisted Journey Map Import is included with Journey Management at no additional cost. When should I use AI-Assisted Import instead of building a journey manually? Use AI-Assisted Import when: You already have journeys documented in Excel or PDFs You are migrating journeys from another platform You want to accelerate onboarding, audits, or workshops Build manually when designing a brand-new journey from scratch. Can the feature handle large or complex journey files? Yes. It is designed for enterprise-scale journeys with multiple stages, steps, and lanes. Expanded bulk-import capabilities are on the roadmap to further support large transformation programs. What happens if my file contains unstructured notes or narrative text? The feature works best with structured journey content. If the document is primarily free-form narrative, the AI may not reliably convert it into stages and steps, and manual creation may be recommended. How does this help my team operationally? AI-Assisted Import reduces manual effort and accelerates time-to-value by: Eliminating duplicate journey documentation Standardizing structures across teams Making existing research immediately actionable Turning static files into live, manageable journeys License This feature is available with the following license : Customer Experience Was the article helpful?       "content": "Journey Frameworks Introduction Journey Frameworks help organizations create customer journey maps faster by allowing teams to start with reusable templates instead of building every journey from scratch. Frameworks provide predefined journey structures, phases, and touchpoints that can be reused across projects, teams, and business units. Organizations can also save their own journey maps as frameworks, creating a centralized repository of best practices and approved journey structures. What are Journey Frameworks? Journey Frameworks are reusable journey map templates that help teams standardize journey mapping and accelerate journey creation. Frameworks can be used to: Reduce the time required to create journey maps. Reuse proven journey structures and methodologies. Standardize journey mapping across teams. Preserve organizational best practices. Support journey governance initiatives. Ensure consistency across departments and business units. Journey Management supports two types of frameworks: QuestionPro Frameworks – Frameworks provided by QuestionPro. My Frameworks – Frameworks created by users within your organization. How do I create a journey using a Framework? Navigate to Journey Management. Select the Workspace that contains the board where you want to create the journey. Open the desired Board. Click New Journey. Select one of the following options: Organization Frameworks QuestionPro Frameworks Select a framework. Click Create Journey. The new journey map will be created using the selected framework structure. If you select the Default Framework, you can build your journey from scratch. How do I save a journey as a Framework? If you have created a journey map that you would like to reuse in the future, you can save it as an Organization Framework. Open the journey map you want to save. Navigate to Journey Settings. Click Save as Framework. The framework will be added to the Framework Library and will be available for future journey creation. How do I access the Framework Library? From the left navigation menu, click Frameworks. The Framework Library displays all available frameworks How do I manage Frameworks? Users can manage frameworks directly from the Framework Library. Available actions include: View available frameworks. Edit framework names. Edit framework descriptions. Delete frameworks. Reuse frameworks across multiple journey maps. Common Use Cases Create organization-approved journey templates for governance and consistency. Standardize customer lifecycle journeys across teams. Create repeatable onboarding and retention journeys. Scale journey mapping programs across departments. Reuse successful journey structures across regions, products, and customer segments. Accelerate journey creation for consultants and agency teams. Frequently Asked Questions Can I modify a journey after creating it from a framework? Yes. Once a journey map is created from a framework, it becomes an independent journey and can be modified as needed. Can I create my own frameworks? Yes. Any existing journey map can be saved as an Organization Framework. Can multiple teams use the same framework? Yes. Frameworks are designed to be reused across teams, departments, and business units. Can I edit the contents of a framework? No. Currently, users can only edit the framework name and description. To change the framework structure, create a new journey with the desired changes and save it as a new framework. What happens if I update a framework? Changes apply only to the framework metadata (name and description). Existing journey maps are not affected. What happens if I delete a framework? Deleting a framework removes it from the Framework Library but does not impact any existing journey maps that were created from it. Best Practices Create frameworks for commonly used journey structures. Establish organization-approved frameworks to support governance. Use clear framework names and descriptions. Maintain separate frameworks for different customer segments or use cases. Use frameworks to accelerate onboarding for new team members.       "content": "Import Tasks via Excel The Import Tasks via Excel feature allows you to bring in tasks from external sources directly into your initiatives in the Journey Management Platform. This helps you quickly migrate existing task data, assign owners and contributors, and maintain continuity across projects without manual entry. What is Import Tasks via Excel? Import Tasks via Excel lets you upload external task data in bulk and automatically create tasks within your initiative. You can include details such as Task Name, Owner, Contributors, Due Date, and Status. Existing users in your organization are automatically assigned, while new users are added as sub-accounts under your organization, ensuring smooth integration of external data. How do I import external tasks using Excel? To import tasks from an external Excel file, follow these steps: Go to Initiatives under the Planning and Outcomes section in the Journey Management Platform. Go to the Initiative where you want to add tasks. Click the Import Tasks button. In the pop-up window: Download the sample template first. Fill in your task details (Task Name, Owner, Contributors, Due Date, Status) in the template. Once complete, upload the filled template to import your tasks. Click Import to add all tasks from the Excel file into your initiative automatically. What columns are required in the Excel template? Your Excel file should include the following columns: Task Name – Name of the task. Owner – Person responsible for the task. Contributors – Team members involved in the task. Due Date – Task deadline Status – Current status of the task (e.g., Pending, In progress, Completed). What happens after import? After import: All external tasks are added to the selected initiative. Owners and Contributors are assigned automatically if they exist in your organization. New sub-accounts are created for any external users not in your organization. You can edit tasks, update owners, contributors, due dates, and status just like any other task in the platform. Frequently Asked Questions The following questions cover common usage scenarios, best practices, and troubleshooting for importing tasks from external sources. Do I need to use a specific template? Yes. Using the provided sample template ensures all required columns are included and properly formatted. This minimizes import errors and guarantees correct task assignment. Can I import tasks for users not in my organization? Yes. External users specified as Owners or Contributors will be automatically added as sub-accounts under your organization. Will importing tasks overwrite existing tasks? No. Imported tasks are added as new tasks in the selected initiative. Existing tasks remain unchanged. Can I edit tasks after import? Yes. Once tasks are imported, you can edit task names, assign new owners or contributors, update statuses, and adjust due dates. What should I do if the import fails? Check that your Excel file follows the template format, all required columns are filled, and user names match existing organization members. Correct any errors and try importing again.
